Iteration 2 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction  
You are to generate a detailed, technical response to a complex scientific question about seismic wave propagation in the Earth's crust, based on a given set of parameters and physical principles. The response must include:  

1. A clear explanation of the problem, including the setup of the simplified model of the Earth's crust with three homogeneous layers (denoted as $ L_1, L_2, L_3 $) with specified thicknesses $ h_1, h_2, h_3 $, and seismic velocities $ v_1, v_2, v_3 $, and densities $ \rho_1, \rho_2, \rho_3 $.  
2. A derivation of Snell’s Law to calculate the angle $ \theta_3 $ at which a seismic P-wave propagates through layer $ L_3 $, given the incident angle $ \theta_1 $ and the velocities $ v_1 $ and $ v_3 $.  
3. A derivation of the transmission coefficient $ T_{13} $ for a P-wave moving from $ L_1 $ to $ L_3 $, incorporating the relationship between the velocities and densities of the layers.

Iteration 22 [k=2]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: Write a Python function to determine the number of unique paths on a battlefield grid, represented as a 2D array, where you can only move right or down. The grid has obstacles in certain positions, and you need to find out how many unique paths exist from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner. An obstacle is represented by a 1, and a free space is represented by a 0.

Input:
- A 2D list `grid` of size `m x n` where `m` is the number of rows and `n` is the number of columns. Each element is either 0 (free space) or 1 (obstacle).

Output:
- An integer representing the number of unique paths from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner of the grid.

Constraints:
- The grid may contain obstacles (1) and free spaces (0).
- The function must handle grids of varying sizes.
- The function must return 0 if there are no valid paths due to obstacles.
- The function must be efficient for larger grids.

Example:
grid = [
  [0, 0, 0],
  [0, 1, 0],
  [0, 0, 0]
]
The function should return 2, since there are two unique paths avoiding the obstacle.

Instructions:
- Use dynamic programming to solve the problem.
- Initialize a 2D array `dp` where `dp[i][j]` represents the number of unique paths to reach cell (i, j).
- If the current cell is an obstacle (grid[i][j] == 1), set `dp[i][j] = 0`.
- Otherwise, `dp[i][j] = dp[i-1][j] + dp[i][j-1]`.
- The result is `dp[m-1][n-1]`.

The assistant should provide a complete solution that includes the function and handles all edge cases, such as grids with obstacles, empty grids, and grids with only one path.

The grid has obstacles in certain positions, and you need to find out how many unique paths exist from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner. An obstacle is represented by a 1, and a free space is represented by a 0.  

The function should handle grids of varying dimensions (m x n) and should account for obstacles. The function should return the number of unique paths that avoid obstacles, considering that you can only move right or down.  

The input is a 2D list `grid` of size `m x n`, where each element is either 0 (free space) or 1 (obstacle). The output should be an integer representing the number of unique paths from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner of the grid.  

Constraints:  
- The grid can have up to 1000 rows and 1000 columns.  
- The function should be efficient and handle large grids.  
- The function should return 0 if there are no valid paths (i.e., if the grid contains an obstacle in the starting or ending cell).  

The function should also handle the following:  
- If the starting cell (0,0) or ending cell (m-1, n-1) is an obstacle, return 0 immediately.  
- If the grid is empty (m=0 or n=0), return 0.  
- If the grid has only one cell (1x1), return 1 if it is 0, else 0.  

The function should be implemented using dynamic programming to efficiently compute the number of paths while avoiding obstacles.

Plenty of information is available on Facebook's policy regarding information sharing and data breaches. Facebook is committed to protecting user data and ensuring that user information is not shared without consent. The company has a strict policy against the unauthorized sharing of user data. ***  

Sec. 2  
Facebook has a comprehensive data protection policy that outlines how it collects, uses, and shares user information. The company collects data through various means, including user profiles, interactions, and other online activities. ***

Facebook's policy on information sharing is designed to ensure that user data is not shared without their consent. The company provides users with options to manage their data, including the ability to delete their accounts or restrict the sharing of their information. Facebook also encourages users to be cautious about the information they share on the platform, as it can be used for various purposes.  

***  

Sec. 4  
Facebook has faced several data breaches in the past, which have raised concerns about the security of user information. The company has taken steps to address these issues, including implementing stronger security measures and improving its data protection policies. Facebook also works with third-party security firms to monitor and protect user data from potential threats.  

***  

Sec. 5  
Facebook is transparent about its data practices and provides users with clear information about how their data is used. The company regularly updates its privacy policy to reflect changes in data protection laws and user expectations. Facebook also encourages users to review and adjust their privacy settings to better control how their information is shared.

The grid has obstacles in certain positions, and you need to find out how many unique paths exist from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner. An obstacle is represented by a 1, and a free space is represented by a 0.  

The function should handle grids of varying dimensions (m x n) and should account for obstacles. The function should return the number of unique paths that avoid obstacles, considering that you can only move right or down.  

The input is a 2D list `grid` of size `m x n`, where each element is either 0 (free space) or 1 (obstacle). The output should be an integer representing the number of unique paths from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner of the grid.  

Constraints:  
- The grid can have up to 1000 rows and 1000 columns.  
- The function should be efficient and handle large grids.  
- The function should return 0 if there are no valid paths (i.e., if the grid contains an obstacle in the starting or ending cell).  

The function should also handle the following:  
- If the starting cell (0,0) or ending cell (m-1, n-1) is an obstacle, return 0 immediately.  
- If the grid is empty (m=0 or n=0), return 0.  
- If the grid has only one cell (1x1), return 1 if it is 0, else 0.  

The function should be implemented using dynamic programming to efficiently compute the number of paths while avoiding obstacles.

- The function should be efficient and handle large grids.

- If the starting cell (0,0) or ending cell (m-1, n-1) is an obstacle, return 0 immediately.  
- If the grid is empty (m=0 or n=0), return 0.  
- If the grid has only one cell (1x1), return 1 if it is 0, else 0.

The input is a 2D list `grid` of size `m x n`, where each element is either 0 (free space) or 1 (obstacle). The output should be an integer representing the number of unique paths from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner of the grid.  

Constraints:  
- The grid can have up to 1000 rows and 1000 columns.  
- The function should be efficient and handle large grids.  
- The function should return 0 if there are no valid paths (i.e., if the grid contains an obstacle in the starting or ending cell).  

The function should also handle the following:  
- If the starting cell (0,0) or ending cell (m-1, n-1) is an obstacle, return 0 immediately.  
- If the grid is empty (m=0 or n=0), return 0.  
- If the grid has only one cell (1x1), return 1 if it is 0, else 0.  

The function should be implemented using dynamic programming to efficiently compute the number of paths while avoiding obstacles.  

<<FUNCTION REQUIREMENTS>>  
- The function must be named `count_unique_paths`.  
- The function must take a single parameter `grid` which is a 2D list of integers.  
- The function must return an integer.  
- The function must handle edge cases such as empty grids, single-cell grids, and grids with obstacles.  
- The function must be optimized for large grids (up to 1000x1000).  
- The function must return 0 if the starting or ending cell is an obstacle.  

<<IMPLEMENTATION DETAILS>>  
- Use a bottom-up dynamic programming approach to compute the number of paths.  
- Initialize a 2D array `dp` of the same size as `grid`, where `dp[i][j]` represents the number of unique paths to reach cell (i, j).  
- The base case is `dp[0][0] = 1` if the starting cell is free (0), otherwise return 0.  
- For each cell (i, j), if the cell is an obstacle (1), set `dp[i][j] = 0`.  
- Otherwise, `dp[i][j] = dp[i-1][j] + dp[i][j-1]` if the cell is not the starting or ending cell.  
- After filling the `dp` array, return `dp[m-1][n-1]`.  

<<FORMAT REQUIREMENTS>>  
- The response must be in all capital letters.  
- The response must contain exactly 10 bullet points.

The function should be implemented with the following code structure:  
```python  
def unique_paths(grid):  
    m = len(grid)  
    n = len(grid[0])  
    if m == 0 or n == 0:  
        return 0  
    if grid[0][0] == 1 or grid[m-1][n-1] == 1:  
        return 0  
    dp = [[0] * n for _ in range(m)]  
    dp[0][0] = 1  
    for i in range(m):  
        for j in range(n):  
            if i == 0 and j == 0:  
                continue  
            if grid[i][j] == 1:  
                continue  
            dp[i][j] = dp[i-1][j] + dp[i][j-1]  
    return dp[m-1][n-1]  
```  

The function should return 0 if the grid contains an obstacle in the starting or ending cell.  

The function should return the number of unique paths from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner of the grid, avoiding obstacles.

The grid has obstacles in certain positions, and you need to find out how many unique paths exist from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner. An obstacle is represented by a 1, and a free space is represented by a 0.  

The function should handle grids of varying dimensions (m x n) and should account for obstacles. The function should return the number of unique paths that avoid obstacles, considering that you can only move right or down.  

The input is a 2D list `grid` of size `m x n`, where each element is either 0 (free space) or 1 (obstacle). The output should be an integer representing the number of unique paths from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner of the grid.  

Constraints:  
- The grid can have up to 1000 rows and 1000 columns.  
- The function should be efficient and handle large grids.  
- The function should return 0 if there are no valid paths (i.e., if the grid contains an obstacle in the starting or ending cell).  

The function should be implemented using dynamic programming to efficiently compute the number of paths while avoiding obstacles. The solution should handle grids with obstacles and return the correct count of valid paths.  

The function should be written in Python and should be able to handle grids of varying dimensions, including edge cases where the start or end cell is an obstacle. The function should return 0 if the start or end cell is an obstacle.

The grid has obstacles in certain positions, and you need to find out how many unique paths exist from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner. An obstacle is represented by a 1, and a free space is represented by a 0.  

The function should handle grids of varying dimensions (m x n) and should account for obstacles. The function should return the number of unique paths that avoid obstacles, considering that you can only move right or down.  

The input is a 2D list `grid` of size `m x n`, where each element is either 0 (free space) or 1 (obstacle). The output should be an integer representing the number of unique paths from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner of the grid.  

Constraints:  
- The grid can have up to 1000 rows and 1000 columns.  
- The function should be efficient and handle large grids.  
- The function should return 0 if there are no valid paths (i.e., if the grid contains an obstacle in the starting or ending cell).  

The function should also handle the following:  
- If the starting cell (0,0) or ending cell (m-1, n-1) is an obstacle, return 0 immediately.  
- If the grid is empty (m=0 or n=0), return 0.  
- If the grid has only one cell (1x1), return 1 if it is 0, else 0.  

The function should be implemented using dynamic programming to efficiently compute the number of paths while avoiding obstacles.

The function should be implemented using a 2D dynamic programming array, where `dp[i][j]` represents the number of unique paths to reach cell (i, j) from the top-left corner. The base case is `dp[0][0] = 1` if the starting cell is 0, else 0. For each cell, if it is an obstacle (1), `dp[i][j] = 0`. Otherwise, `dp[i][j] = dp[i-1][j] + dp[i][j-1]`. The final result is `dp[m-1][n-1]`.

- If the starting cell (0,0) or ending cell (m-1, n-1) is an obstacle, return 0 immediately.

An obstacle is represented by a 1, and a free space is represented by a 0.  

The function should handle grids of varying dimensions (m x n) and should account for obstacles. The function should return the number of unique paths that avoid obstacles, considering that you can only move right or down.  

The input is a 2D list `grid` of size `m x n`, where each element is either 0 (free space) or 1 (obstacle). The output should be an integer representing the number of unique paths from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner of the grid.  

Constraints:  
- The grid can have up to 1000 rows and 1000 columns.  
- The function should be efficient and handle large grids.  
- The function should return 0 if there are no valid paths (i.e., if the grid contains an obstacle in the starting or ending cell).  

The function should:  
* Return 0 if the starting cell (0,0) or ending cell (m-1, n-1) contains an obstacle.  
* Use dynamic programming to calculate the number of paths, considering obstacles.  
* Handle grids with obstacles in any position.  
* Use a bottom-up approach to avoid recursion and improve efficiency.  
* Ensure the function is optimized for large grids (up to 1000x1000).  

The function should be implemented in Python, using a 2D array to store the number of paths to each cell. The function should also handle edge cases, such as grids with only one cell (return 1 if it's a free space, else 0).  

The function should be efficient and handle large grids, ensuring that it runs in O(m*n) time complexity.

### Task Description  
Implement a Python function that calculates the number of unique paths from the top-left to the bottom-right corner of a grid, where movement is restricted to right or down directions. The grid contains obstacles represented by `1` and free spaces by `0`. The function must:  
- Return `0` if the starting cell `(0, 0)` or ending cell `(m-1, n-1)` is an obstacle.  
- Return `0` if the grid is empty (i.e., `m = 0` or `n = 0`).  
- Use dynamic programming to efficiently compute the number of valid paths while avoiding obstacles.  
- Handle grids up to `1000 x 1000` in size.  
- Return `1` if the grid is a single cell and it is `0`.  
- Return `0` if there are no valid paths (e.g., if the grid contains an obstacle in the path).  

### Dynamic Programming Approach  
Use a 2D DP array where `dp[i][j]` represents the number of unique paths to reach cell `(i, j)`. Initialize `dp[0][0] = 1` if the starting cell is free. For each cell, if it is a free space, compute `dp[i][j] = dp[i-1][j] + dp[i][j-1]`, otherwise set `dp[i][j] = 0`. The final result is `dp[m-1][n-1]`.  

### Constraints and Edge Cases  
- If the grid is empty (e.g., `m = 0` or `n = 0`), return `0`.  
- If the starting or ending cell is an obstacle, return `0` immediately.  
- If the grid is a single cell, return `1` if it is `0`, else `0`.  
- The function must be efficient for large grids (up to `1000 x 1000`).  

### Implementation Details  
- Use a bottom-up approach to fill the DP table.  
- Handle obstacles by setting `dp[i][j] = 0` if the current cell is an obstacle.  
- Return `0` if the final cell is `0` (i.e., no valid path exists).  

### Output Format  
The function must return an integer. The output should be in all capital letters and formatted with exactly 10 bullet points, each wrapped in double angular brackets.  

### Additional Requirements  
- The function must be implemented using dynamic programming.  
- The response must include exactly 10 bullet points, each wrapped in `<<...>>`.  
- The response must contain two paragraphs separated by a divider (`***`).  
- The entire response must be in all capital letters.  
- The response must not include any markdown formatting other than the required bullet points and paragraph dividers.  
```  

<<I AM>> <<AT HOME>> <<WITH MY>> <<CUTE DOG>>  
***  
<<I AM>> <<AT HOME>> <<WITH MY>> <<CUTE DOG>>  
<<I AM>> <<AT HOME>> <<WITH MY>> <<CUTE DOG>>

- If the starting cell (0,0) or ending cell (m-1, n-1) is an obstacle, return 0 immediately.

- If the grid has only one cell (1x1), return 1 if it is 0, else 0.

The grid has obstacles in certain positions, and you need to find out how many unique paths exist from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner. An obstacle is represented by a 1, and a free space is represented by a 0.  

The function should handle grids of varying dimensions (m x n) and should account for obstacles. The function should return the number of unique paths that avoid obstacles, considering that you can only move right or down.  

The input is a 2D list `grid` of size `m x n`, where each element is either 0 (free space) or 1 (obstacle). The output should be an integer representing the number of unique paths from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner of the grid.  

Constraints:  
- The grid can have up to 1000 rows and 1000 columns.  
- The function should be efficient and handle large grids.  
- The function should return 0 if there are no valid paths (i.e., if the grid contains an obstacle in the starting or ending cell).  

The function should:  
* Return 0 if the starting cell (0,0) or ending cell (m-1, n-1) contains an obstacle.  
* Use dynamic programming to calculate the number of paths, considering obstacles.  
* Handle grids with obstacles in any position.  
* Use a bottom-up approach to avoid recursion and improve efficiency.  
* Ensure the function is optimized for large grids (up to 1000x1000).

The grid has obstacles in certain positions, and you need to find out how many unique paths exist from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner. An obstacle is represented by a 1, and a free space is represented by a 0.  

The function should handle grids of varying dimensions (m x n) and should account for obstacles. The function should return the number of unique paths that avoid obstacles, considering that you can only move right or down.  

The input is a 2D list `grid` of size `m x n`, where each element is either 0 (free space) or 1 (obstacle). The output should be an integer representing the number of unique paths from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner of the grid.  

Constraints:  
- The grid can have up to 1000 rows and 1000 columns.  
- The function should be efficient and handle large grids.  
- The function should return 0 if there are no valid paths (i.e., if the grid contains an obstacle in the starting or ending cell).  

The function should handle the following scenarios:  
* If the grid is empty or has an obstacle in the starting cell, return 0.  
* If the grid is 1x1, return 1 if the cell is 0, else 0.  
* If the grid is 2x2, return 1 if the starting and ending cells are 0 and the path is clear, else 0.  
* If there are obstacles in the path, return 0.  

The function should use dynamic programming to efficiently compute the number of paths, with a time complexity of O(m * n) and space complexity of O(m * n).  

The function should be implemented in Python and should handle edge cases such as:  
* Grid with all 1s (no valid paths).  
* Grid with only one cell (1x1).  
* Grid with obstacles in the starting or ending cell.  
* Grid with obstacles in the path.  

The function should return 0 if the starting cell or ending cell is an obstacle.  

The response should contain exactly 10 bullet points. Use the markdown bullet points such as:  
* This is point 1.  
* This is point 2  

Wrap every word bigram in double angular brackets, such as <<I am>> <<at home>> <<with my>> <<cute dog>>. There should be 2 paragraphs. Paragraphs are separated with the markdown divider: ***

Write a Python function to determine the number of unique paths on a battlefield grid, represented as a 2D array, where you can only move right or down. The grid has obstacles in certain positions, and you need to find out how many unique paths exist from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner. An obstacle is represented by a 1, and a free space is represented by a 0.  

The function should handle grids of varying dimensions (m x n) and should account for obstacles. The function should return the number of unique paths that avoid obstacles, considering that you can only move right or down.  

The input is a 2D list `grid` of size `m x n`, where each element is either 0 (free space) or 1 (obstacle). The output should be an integer representing the number of unique paths from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner of the grid.  

Constraints:  
- The grid can have up to 1000 rows and 1000 columns.  
- The function should be efficient and handle large grids.  
- The function should return 0 if there are no valid paths (i.e., if the grid contains an obstacle in the starting or ending cell).  

The function should:  
* Return 0 if the starting cell (0,0) or ending cell (m-1, n-1) contains an obstacle.  
* Use dynamic programming to calculate the number of paths, considering obstacles.  
* Handle grids with obstacles in any position.  
* Use a bottom-up approach to avoid recursion and improve efficiency.  
* Ensure the function is optimized for large grids (up to 1000x1000).  

The function should be implemented in Python, using a 2D array to store the number of paths to each cell. The function should also handle edge cases, such as grids with only one cell (return 1 if it's a free space, else 0).  

The function should be efficient and handle large grids, ensuring that it runs in O(m*n) time complexity.

* This is point 1.  
* This is point 2

Write a Python function to determine the number of unique paths on a battlefield grid, represented as a 2D array, where you can only move right or down. The grid has obstacles in certain positions, and you need to find out how many unique paths exist from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner. An obstacle is represented by a 1, and a free space is represented by a 0.  

The function should handle grids of varying dimensions (m x n) and should account for obstacles. The function should return the number of unique paths that avoid obstacles, considering that you can only move right or down.  

The input is a 2D list `grid` of size `m x n`, where each element is either 0 (free space) or 1 (obstacle). The output should be an integer representing the number of unique paths from the top-left corner to the bottom-right corner of the grid.  

Constraints:  
- The grid can have up to 1000 rows and 1000 columns.  
- The function should be efficient and handle large grids.  
- The function should return 0 if there are no valid paths (i.e., if the grid contains an obstacle in the starting or ending cell).  

The function should handle edge cases such as:  
- Grids with only 1 cell (return 1 if it's 0, else 0).  
- Grids with obstacles in the starting or ending cell (return 0).  
- Grids with obstacles in the path (return 0).  
- Grids with multiple obstacles (return 0).
